            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-paperback">read-owned-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=guy-gavriel-kay">guy-gavriel-kay</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92602852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7604893038742075839">For most of this read, I thought I was holding another 5-star GGK book. The political manueverings and intrigue are fantastic, as are the twists and turns that the protagonist, Caius Crispus, faces. The individual pieces in the political puzzle are intriguing too, from the Empress Arixana and the Emperor Valerius to the Queen Gisel, and the First Stratego Leontus and his seductive aristocrat bride.<br/><br/>The book beautifully sets up the sequel, <i>Lord of Emperors</i>, which now goes to the top of my read pil</span>
  <span id="freeText7604893038742075839" style="display:none">For most of this read, I thought I was holding another 5-star GGK book. The political manueverings and intrigue are fantastic, as are the twists and turns that the protagonist, Caius Crispus, faces. The individual pieces in the political puzzle are intriguing too, from the Empress Arixana and the Emperor Valerius to the Queen Gisel, and the First Stratego Leontus and his seductive aristocrat bride.<br /><br />The book beautifully sets up the sequel, <i>Lord of Emperors</i>, which now goes to the top of my read pile. I do feel that my rating of this dropped to a 4-star because of that set up. Not in itself, but in the need for it. The last chapter of this book was quite a wind down from the intrigue that I'd been served for so many pages. It felt like a wrap up, but one that wasn't going to answer any questions. I already knew there was a second part, so I wasn't too concerned. Especially since I have a copy of it as well. But as a singular work on its own merit, <i>Sailing to Sarantium</i> suffers a little for the ending. I suspect that I'll be much more satisfied with the ending of the next book and the duology itself.<br /><br />This book does serve notice that I have indeed been overlooking the work of Guy Gavriel Kay for too long. It is only in the last year and a half that I've been reading him at all, and each book reinforces this thought. <i>Tigana</i> was my first and I gave it 5 stars. Then, earlier this year, I read <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> and wanted to give it 6 stars. As I read through this one, I felt sure it would rank right between the previous 5-star ratings, being a little better than <i>Tigana</i> but not quite as wonderful as <i>Arbonne</i>, but in the end <i>Tigana</i> had a much more satisfactory wrap up.<br /><br />Should I penalize a book that is obviously meant to be the set up for a second volume? Perhaps not. It may be that when I do read <i>Lord of Emperors</i> I may feel the need to come back and revisit this decision. It is true that Kay set the bar pretty high with the other books I've read, so half a story won't be able to stand up against them. But once I've completed the duology, we'll see how the total sum of the package compares.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7604893038742075839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2116794702" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2116794702" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2116794702?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451463517" href="/book/show/8292126-sailing-to-sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2116794702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15591042969463227825"><i>”To say of a man that he was sailing to Sarantium was to say that his life was on the cusp of change: poised for emergent greatness, brilliance, fortune – or else at the very precipice of a final and absolute fall as he met something too vast for his capacity.”</i><br/><br/>Caius Crispus is a man, a mosaicist by trade, who has been living under the shadow of grief after losing his wife and two daughters to the Plague. His life is only about his work now. The decision of an emperor in a neighboring country to </span>
  <span id="freeText15591042969463227825" style="display:none"><i>”To say of a man that he was sailing to Sarantium was to say that his life was on the cusp of change: poised for emergent greatness, brilliance, fortune – or else at the very precipice of a final and absolute fall as he met something too vast for his capacity.”</i><br /><br />Caius Crispus is a man, a mosaicist by trade, who has been living under the shadow of grief after losing his wife and two daughters to the Plague. His life is only about his work now. The decision of an emperor in a neighboring country to build an ornate sanctuary sets off a chain of events that lead Crispin - decision by decision, by decision (for in such ways is a man’s life made) - to the imperial city of Sarantium. <br /><br />Kay’s writing is always elegant and beautiful and this book is no exception. If you are looking for action packed stories, then Kay is not the author for you. His work is too meticulously and deliberately constructed in such a way as to allow the reader to wander in and among the words and through the paragraphs and across the pages at leisure. These are words to be savored, not rushed through or skimmed over.<br /><br />Strong characters are another hallmark of Kay’s writing. He gives readers just enough context for and insight into his characters that they feel like actual people. Crispin meets several memorable people during his journey and I found myself laughing with them, fearing for them, rooting for them (or, in some cases, against them).<br /><br />This is the first book in a duology and, based on some other reviews I’d read, I feared a cliffhanger-ish ending. In my opinion, the ending for this book could very well serve as its own stopping point. True, there are some issues with secondary characters that are left in flux but Crispin himself has reached a level of self-awareness and understanding by the end…a new precipice…and anything is possible. That sort of open ending seems very much like actual life to me. None of us knows what tomorrow will bring but we still stride off into each new day hoping for the best. So, in my opinion, it is possible to leave Crispin’s story here. I won’t, of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15591042969463227825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_474618061" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474618061" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474618061?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143194040" href="/book/show/27064656-sailing-to-sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=when-words-collide">when-words-collide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=canadian-eh">canadian-eh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=2020-reading-list">2020-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=public-library">public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1990s">z-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=november-2020">november-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474618061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3938686755762839201">Sinking into a Guy Gavriel Kay historical fantasy is like immersing myself in a warm, fragrant bath, lovely and comforting. His worldview meshes with mine so well, he is truly the perfect author match for me. Now that I have finished this volume, I have only three unread books of his left and this distresses me. What will I do until he publishes the next? Well, begin a re-reading cycle, yes, but there is no feeling like the first experience of a GGK novel.<br/><br/>Well, I shall persevere. Because this au</span>
  <span id="freeText3938686755762839201" style="display:none">Sinking into a Guy Gavriel Kay historical fantasy is like immersing myself in a warm, fragrant bath, lovely and comforting. His worldview meshes with mine so well, he is truly the perfect author match for me. Now that I have finished this volume, I have only three unread books of his left and this distresses me. What will I do until he publishes the next? Well, begin a re-reading cycle, yes, but there is no feeling like the first experience of a GGK novel.<br /><br />Well, I shall persevere. Because this author writes main characters who are decent men like Caius Crispin. He may be cranky (he has reasons) and he may take risks, but he is kind to those who he has power over, perhaps the most telling measure of a man. In addition to decent men, Kay writes women as real people (we are, you know), with the same aspirations and emotions as his male characters. They aren't perplexing enigmas, they aren't cardboard cut-outs, they are fully realized people. This is the major reason that I adore Mr. Kay's fiction.<br /><br />The other main reason is his treatment of the religious aspect of life. Crispen comes face to face with a Pagan god, he is knocked on his back by a spectacular Jaddite mosaic, and both of these experiences feel absolutely real to me. I feel his awe right along with him. Aspiring to be a happy Pagan myself, feeling a lot of sympathy for such things, this aspect of the story delights me. (This is why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/903.The_Egypt_Game" title="The Egypt Game by Zilpha Keatley Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Egypt Game</a> grabbed me firmly as a tween and why the King Arthur cycle continues to speak to me so loudly today, I am just a sucker for pre-Christian religions.) <br /><br />As Crispin plans his grand mosaic, I am reminded of another favourite book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/265767.What_s_Bred_in_the_Bone__Cornish_Trilogy___2_" title="What's Bred in the Bone (Cornish Trilogy, #2) by Robertson Davies" rel="nofollow noopener">What's Bred in the Bone</a> by Robertson Davies. It's main character, Francis Cornish, also creates a very personal masterpiece, a painting done in Old Master style, but featuring people and symbols peculiar to the artist. He smuggles his own mythology into it and creates something extraordinary, just as I expect Crispen will do in this sanctuary.<br /><br />I both look forward to and dread reading the second half of this tale. On one hand I want to spend more time in this world with these people. On the other hand, then the adventure will be over. The best books leave me feeling torn this way. <br /><br /><b>Book number 383 of my Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Reading Project.</b><br /><br />Cross posted at my blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.com/2020/11/sailing-to-sarantium-guy-gavriel-kay.html">https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3938686755762839201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1661412967" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1661412967?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780684851693" href="/book/show/821488.Sailing_to_Sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1661412967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5994048737865658188">8.5/10<br/><br/>I have to say before I started <i>The Sarantine Mosaic</i> I was a bit worried that I might not like so much Guy Gavriel Kay’s more “historical” based stories, but after reading <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609181260' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Last Light of the Sun</a>
</i>, which I liked it a lot, my interest on this duology began to change and of course Kay has done here a really great story.<br/>Inspired by some events on the 6th century in Byzantium Kay has made an incredible world, full with wonderful characters and with his writing being, simply, <i>amazing</i>.<br/><br/>The s</span>
  <span id="freeText5994048737865658188" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />I have to say before I started <i>The Sarantine Mosaic</i> I was a bit worried that I might not like so much Guy Gavriel Kay’s more “historical” based stories, but after reading <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609181260" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Last Light of the Sun</a>
</i>, which I liked it a lot, my interest on this duology began to change and of course Kay has done here a really great story.<br />Inspired by some events on the 6th century in Byzantium Kay has made an incredible world, full with wonderful characters and with his writing being, simply, <i>amazing</i>.<br /><br />The story is mostly centered on Crispin, a simple mosaicict, who when one day is summoned by the Emperor to decorate the Sanctuary of Jad (something similar to Christ) he’ll have to travel to the far Sarantium. In the road to Sarantium though he will come against many strange things and gods that he didn’t believe that were real and will change his life forever; but this is only beginning.<br />As he arrives in Sarantium Crispin will find himself in a world totally different from his own and he’ll have to face not only the cunning Emperor but also the intrigues and machinations that follow the court, and the only thing that can save him is only himself.<br /><br />What really stands out in this book is not really the story itself but the characters and the world-building that Kay has made, and even though there are in an imaginary world sometimes he makes them seem all very “real”, and that is the reason, as I believe, why this book is so great.<br />Of course the story doesn’t have many fantasy elements but the way Kay handles them makes, I think, all the deference as he weaves through them with his wonderful writing, and let me tell you that I haven’t loved him that much since <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383526782" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tigana</a>
</i>.<br /><br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Πριν πιάσω αυτή την δυλογία πρέπει να πω ότι ήμουν κάπως επιφυλακτικός καθώς δεν ήμουν σίγουρος αν θα μου άρεσε τόσο το πιο «ιστορικό» κομμάτι του Kay, όμως μετά το Last Light of the Sun, που άρεσε αρκετά, το ενδιαφέρον μου άρχισε να αλλάζει και φυσικά ο Kay εδώ έχει κάνει μια εξαιρετική ιστορία.<br />Βασισμένος λοιπόν σε γεγονότα από τον 6ο αιώνα στο Βυζάντιο, ο Kay έχει φτιάξει έναν πραγματικά απίστευτο κόσμο, γεμάτο με υπέροχους χαρακτήρες αλλά και με την γραφή του, απλά, να μαγεύει.<br /><br />Η ιστορία επικεντρώνεται κυρίως στον Crispin, έναν απλό τεχνίτη μωσαϊκών, που όταν μια μέρα κληθεί από τον Αυτοκράτορα για να διακοσμήσει τον ναό του Jad (κάτι ανάλογο του Χριστού) θα πρέπει να ταξιδέψει στο μακρινό Sarantium. Στην πορεία του ταξιδιού του όμως θα βρεθεί αντιμέτωπος με πολλά περίεργα πράγματα και θεούς που δεν πίστευε ποτέ του ότι υπήρχαν και θα του αλλάξουν την ζωή του για πάντα· αλλά αυτό είναι μόνο η αρχή.<br />Φτάνοντας στο Sarantium ο Crispin θα βρεθεί σε έναν εντελώς διαφορετικό κόσμο από τον δικό του και θα πρέπει να αντιμετωπίσει όχι μόνο τον πανούργο Αυτοκράτορα αλλά και τις ίντριγκες και δολοπλοκίες που ακολουθούν το παλάτι, και το μόνο που μπορεί να τον σώσει είναι μόνο ο εαυτός του.<br /><br />Αυτό που ξεχωρίζει περισσότερο στο βιβλίο δεν είναι τόσο η ιστορία αλλά οι χαρακτήρες και η κοσμπλασία που έχει φτιάξει ο Kay, και παρόλο που είναι σε έναν εντελώς δικό του κόσμο πολλές φορές τα κάνει να φαίνονται όλα πολύ «αληθινά», πράγμα που είναι και ο λόγος που κάνει και το βιβλίο τόσο καλό.<br /><br />Βέβαια τα φανταστικά στοιχεία που έχει προσθέσει δεν είναι πολλά σε αυτό το βιβλίο αλλά ο τρόπος που τα χειρίζεται ο Kay κάνουν, πιστεύω, όλη την διαφορά καθώς «υφαίνει» με την απίστευτη γραφή του, και πρέπει να πω ότι είναι ότι καλύτερο έχω δει από τότε που διάβασα το Tigana. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_601759337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601759337" />
    <a title="Ross" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13012333-ross"><img alt="Ross" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523208735p2/13012333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601759337?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ross" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ross" href="/user/show/13012333-ross">Ross</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451463517" href="/book/show/8292126-sailing-to-sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13012333-ross?shelf=nautical">nautical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601759337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6819349645462344572">Sailing to Sarantium, Book one of "The Sarantine Mosaic" has blown me away and taken me by complete surprise. Iv'e known about Guy Gavriel Kay for a while, often hearing about his amazing use of language, and hearing how he meticulously researches before writing a book. I read on a fellow blogger's site that this is the perfect place to get introduced to Kay's style. I'm sooo glad I decided to give this book a shot!<br/><br/>Sailing to Sarantium is the first book of a duology and it combines elements of H</span>
  <span id="freeText6819349645462344572" style="display:none">Sailing to Sarantium, Book one of "The Sarantine Mosaic" has blown me away and taken me by complete surprise. Iv'e known about Guy Gavriel Kay for a while, often hearing about his amazing use of language, and hearing how he meticulously researches before writing a book. I read on a fellow blogger's site that this is the perfect place to get introduced to Kay's style. I'm sooo glad I decided to give this book a shot!<br /><br />Sailing to Sarantium is the first book of a duology and it combines elements of High Fantasy with Historical Fiction. The setting is an alternate Byzantine world, and it is incredibly well done. I'm still not sure how Kay managed to fit so much story in only 400 pages, with so many characters. One of the things that I enjoyed most while reading this book was the clever pace. Kay bounces from character to character but interweaves their stories brilliantly and when they finally come together you can't help but admit how flawless it all felt. There was also some sex in this book and I have to say it was written very well... I won't go into further detail there!<br /><br />The characters were exceptional. Caius Crispus, a mosaicist is summoned to Sarantium to help create a sanctuary for the emperor and he carries an important message from the queen in his homeland. Along his way to the fabled city he meets a slave girl, (who was one of my favorites) a faithful guide named Vargos, a mysterious alchemist, and a rowdy Soldier. In the city of Sarantium we meet other unique characters including a chariot racer, a chef's apprentice, slimy senators, and a mysterious Empress.<br /><br />If you haven't read Kay yet, then I insist you do. His use of language and dialogue is beautiful and reminded me of R. Scott Bakker. Fans of High Fantasy, Dark Fantasy, Historical Fiction and dare I say Exotic Fantasy will have a lot to like. I have book number two sitting in front of me and I'm very excited to see the conclusion of this powerful story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6819349645462344572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_418688575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/418688575" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418688575?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418688575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15199091212110535183">The new emperor in Sarantium has a lot to atone for, so he’s building a grand chapel to his god and calling the most famous artisans in the surrounding regions to come work for him. Crispin, a mosaicist from a neighboring country, is one of these. Unhappy since his wife and children died, Crispin doesn’t think he has much to live for anymore, and he doesn’t want to go to Sarantium. But when his young queen, who sits her throne precariously, asks Crispin to carry a secret proposal to the already-</span>
  <span id="freeText15199091212110535183" style="display:none">The new emperor in Sarantium has a lot to atone for, so he’s building a grand chapel to his god and calling the most famous artisans in the surrounding regions to come work for him. Crispin, a mosaicist from a neighboring country, is one of these. Unhappy since his wife and children died, Crispin doesn’t think he has much to live for anymore, and he doesn’t want to go to Sarantium. But when his young queen, who sits her throne precariously, asks Crispin to carry a secret proposal to the already-married emperor of Sarantium, Crispin is duty-bound. Now he is “sailing to Sarantium,” which means that he’s leaving everything behind to start a promising new life. Along the way, he befriends an alchemist with strange powers, a young woman who’s about to be sacrificed to a god, and a foul-mouthed army officer who loves to watch the chariot races. When Crispin gets to Sarantium, he finds that decorating the biggest dome in the world isn’t the hardest part of his job — it’s navigating Sarantium court politics.<br /><br />Sailing to Sarantium, the first book in Guy Gavriel Kay’s duology THE SARANTINE MOSAIC, is a historical fantasy loosely based on the Byzantine Empire. It’s a well-written slow-moving character-driven novel that’s full of the violence, sex, political intrigue, passion, and beauty we expect from Kay. If you’re a fan, you’re bound to enjoy this story. I particularly admired the focus on the art of mosaic — both the technique and the way Crispin and his fellow artisans love beauty and are attuned to the play of light, shadow, and color in their environment. I also loved the alchemist’s craft of creating birds of leather and metal and instilling them with personalities (there’s more to it, and it’s cool, but it’d be spoilery to explain further). This was not only a beautiful idea, but it added a nice touch of humor. I also loved the chariot races.<br /><br />There are several likeable characters in Sailing to Sarantium but they spend more time thinking than doing and they’re really hard to believe in. Like most (maybe all) of Kay’s lead males, Crispin is brilliant, strong, brave, blunt and uncompromising (even when he knows he might be killed for it). The women are even more unbelievable. We’re told that they’re powerful, clever and dangerous, but mostly they go around looking beautiful and haughty, teasing men and speaking in arch tones, and using sex as a weapon. Almost every woman we meet in Sailing to Sarantium, other than Crispin’s mother, tries to seduce Crispin as soon as she meets him, though I’m not sure why.<br /><br />The political intrigue is a bit over the top, too. As soon as Crispin arrives in Sarantium, he’s somehow unwittingly in the middle of all the maneuvering, with all the important people wanting to talk to him privately, seduce him, or murder him. We are repeatedly told how clever, subtle, and nuanced all these people are, but I’m not convinced. It’s not clear why they are scheming. Most of the interesting intrigue seems to have happened in the past and we never feel the immediate significance of it all, which just makes it feel overdramatized.<br /><br />Overall, Sailing to Sarantium is a pleasant story if you’re willing to believe in the characters and the significance of the plot. This was hard for me, but I like Crispin and some of the other characters (e.g., the army officer, the famous chef and his apprentice, and the charioteer) and I’m interested in the mosaic and the birds, so I’m going to move on to the second SARANTINE MOSAIC novel, Lord of Emperors, and hope for a bigger pay-off.<br /><br />I’m listening to Berny Clark narrate Audible Frontier’s recent production of THE SARANTINE MOSAIC. He has an agreeable voice and his dialogue is truly excellent, but some of his narration is slow and lacks inflection. I actually didn’t mind this because I thought it served to tone down the drama, but readers who’ve enjoyed other audio productions of Guy Gavriel Kay’s work, which have had more dynamic readers, may feel differently. I suggest listening to a sample.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/sailing-to-sarantium/">http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15199091212110535183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_800704500" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061059902" href="/book/show/104100.Sailing_to_Sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer800704500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11875834736673330961">This was my first foray into historical fantasy, unless I count the Strategos series of Gordon Doherty, which had a bit of fantasy. I enjoy reading about the Byzantine Empire. I chose this one because of the Byzantine [<i>very</i> thinly-disguised] setting; it was close enough to the real Byzantine Empire for me to make parallels. For much of this book I rated it a 4, but after 3/4 through, I had to lower my rating: partly because of sad developments in the story, but partly because of the excessive in</span>
  <span id="freeText11875834736673330961" style="display:none">This was my first foray into historical fantasy, unless I count the Strategos series of Gordon Doherty, which had a bit of fantasy. I enjoy reading about the Byzantine Empire. I chose this one because of the Byzantine [<i>very</i> thinly-disguised] setting; it was close enough to the real Byzantine Empire for me to make parallels. For much of this book I rated it a 4, but after 3/4 through, I had to lower my rating: partly because of sad developments in the story, but partly because of the excessive intriguing and my dislike of two of the main female characters--the Empress and the High Strategos's wife. The story can be summarized briefly: a Rhodian [read: Roman] mosaicist, Caius Crispus, is commissioned by the Emperor Valerius II [=Justinian] for a mosaic in a large church in the city of Sarantium [=Constantinople]. He and various companions he meets and who join him enroute, arrive in Sarantium. Crispus's sardonic lifelike leather-and-tin avian companion, Linon, was fascinating. They would 'speak' to each other by thought transference. Then we learn about the city and its court intrigue. Sarantium is a dangerous place for Crispus. We leave him on a scaffold in the church, contemplating how he will proceed with the mosaic.<br /><br />I do want to continue with vol. 2 in this series. I enjoyed the journey and detailed descriptions of the city, especially the exciting chariot race between the Green and Blue factions. Crispus and his friends were likeable. If the man on the cover of the copy I read is supposed to be Crispus, he looks nothing like the physical description. From that, I picture Crispus as looking like Vincent van Gogh, only a bit younger and more cheerful than this portrait: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.artble.com/imgs/3/2/c/55784/vincent_van_gogh.jpg">http://www.artble.com/imgs/3/2/c/5578...</a>. The novel was well written and evocative of time and place. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1782540629" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782540629" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1782540629?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007342082" href="/book/show/21079696-sailing-to-sarantium">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782540629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5142188804446415151">I don't think this was as good as Under Heaven, but still, the more I read Kay the more I like him. His works are well written, carefully plotted and usually portray great (and human) characters. Fantasy without magic are not my favourites (even Locke has some magic in it, after all), but I don't find it disturbing in this case. <br/><br/>The biggest flaw for me was that in this case the slow pace did bother me a bit. It hadn't happened with Tigana or Under Heaven, but Sailing to Sarantium was, at least i</span>
  <span id="freeText5142188804446415151" style="display:none">I don't think this was as good as Under Heaven, but still, the more I read Kay the more I like him. His works are well written, carefully plotted and usually portray great (and human) characters. Fantasy without magic are not my favourites (even Locke has some magic in it, after all), but I don't find it disturbing in this case. <br /><br />The biggest flaw for me was that in this case the slow pace did bother me a bit. It hadn't happened with Tigana or Under Heaven, but Sailing to Sarantium was, at least in the first 150 pages, too slow. And a bit confusing. After that I started to enjoy it more and more. It has a great cast of characters and the premise to become one of the best political fantasy I've read in a while. If I had to describe why it bothered me a bit I'd probably say that this book felt a bit more like a prologue rather than the first book of a duology. A great one, and with brilliant moments mind you, but still an introduction to the events, characters and schemes to come. <br /><br />That said I really like Kay's characters. They're human, flawed but likable. Much like with Under Heaven I really appreciated that he choose a normal person as the main character. Someone who ends up being a pawn in a bigger scheme and in spite of himself too, rather than the mighty hero. I also think there's room to see much more of the secondary characters and there are some quite interesting ones. <br /><br />I appreciated the plot, especially towards the end, because it does hint at what's to come. I usually think of Kay's plots as a big tapestry, because of how complex and detailed they are. You can see the bigger picture, but if you come closer you'll see hundreds of little details that actually add meaning to it. <br /><br />Hopefully I'm in for a good sequel. I did have a couple of issues with this one, but overall it's a great premise for a good duology. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5142188804446415151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geoff" href="/user/show/5999881-geoff">Geoff</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5999881-geoff?shelf=canadian">canadian</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106109742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13439200526041525286">This is the first Guy Gavriel Kay book that I have read, and I come away from it having had an enjoyable experience. <br/><br/>I found the world to be very fascinating. It might be even more interesting to people familiar with the history of the Byzantine Empire since this novel takes inspiration of that era/setting (the city of Sarantium taking the place of <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=G4phHwSSing' rel='nofollow noopener'>Constantinople</a>). There is a lot of exposition about life in the city which might bore some people but I found it interesting in this instance. Especi</span>
  <span id="freeText13439200526041525286" style="display:none">This is the first Guy Gavriel Kay book that I have read, and I come away from it having had an enjoyable experience. <br /><br />I found the world to be very fascinating. It might be even more interesting to people familiar with the history of the Byzantine Empire since this novel takes inspiration of that era/setting (the city of Sarantium taking the place of <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=G4phHwSSing" rel="nofollow noopener">Constantinople</a>). There is a lot of exposition about life in the city which might bore some people but I found it interesting in this instance. Especially the culture around the hippodrome races, which Kay seemed to have taken from combining chariot racing and rabid football (soccer) fanaticism. <br /><br />The POV jumps around to a lot of different characters throughout the book and they frequently offer contrasting looks at the key moments in the story. The characters are all pretty likable. Even the so-called antagonists of the story seem like reasonable, albeit ambitious and sometimes reckless, characters.<br /><br />But after finishing the novel, I can't help thinking that the whole thing is just the set up to the climax in the 2nd book. Throughout the book there are allusions to conspiracies or nefarious plans in the background but these are rarely brought to the forefront of the story. Some of those likable characters must be involved in this but apparently everyone is perfectly adept at concealing their true motives from the heroes (and the reader).<br /><br />But thats enough to keep me from reading the sequel, as I enthusiastically look forward to find out how it all plays out. And I will definitely seek out more of Kay's work in the future. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13439200526041525286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1571081016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4542056395172762104">4.5*<br/>The prose was wonderful and rich. The world was so well built and fleshed out. I found the first half of the book where Crispin journeyed to Sarantium the most engaging. The second part dragged at times in my opinion. The ending was less impressive than I was hoping for and thus left me feeling a little underwhelmed. Overall really enjoyed my first GGK book, I have the sequel on hold at the library and will read it very soon.</span>

          </span>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15875450705685779213">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categoriz</span>
  <span id="freeText15875450705685779213" style="display:none">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categorization when possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15875450705685779213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
